    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'

  <span id="freeText18248765691207049133" style="display:none">When the dead come back to haunt the living, Lockwood &amp; Co. step in . . .<br /><br />For more than fifty years, the country has been affected by a horrifying epidemic of ghosts. A number of Psychic Investigations Agencies have sprung up to destroy the dangerous apparitions.<br /><br />Lucy Carlyle, a talented young agent, arrives in London hoping for a notable career. Instead she finds herself joining the smallest, most ramshackle agency in the city, run by the charismatic Anthony Lockwood. When one of their cases goes horribly wrong, Lockwood &amp; Co. have one last chance of redemption. Unfortunately this involves spending the night in one of the most haunted houses in England, and trying to escape alive.<br /><br />Set in a city stalked by spectres, The Screaming Staircase is the first in a chilling new series full of suspense, humour and truly terrifying ghosts. Your nights will never be the same again . . .</span>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">You should definitely give Rivers of London by Ben Aaronovitch a try. The protagonist is a police constable dealing with basically anything supernatur<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">You should definitely give Rivers of London by Ben Aaronovitch a try. The protagonist is a police constable dealing with basically anything supernatural, ghosts included. Lockwood &amp; Co. also reminds me of Mary Stanton's Beaufort &amp; Company series (which I read some ten years ago, so I don't remember much). The protagonist is a lawyer who doesn't really mind dead clients (aka ghosts). <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8498360645911077319">My YA recommendation of the month -- which is not really fair since I read the ARC and it doesn't come out until September -- is Jonathan Stroud's Lockwood & Co.: The Screaming Staircase. You may be familiar with Stroud's earlier series about the genie Bartimaeus, and like Bartimaeus, Lockwood & Co. offers us an alternate modern England -- a brilliantly rendered world in which "the Problem" has inexplicably caused ghosts to run rampant and disrupt the lives of mortals. In this new reality, priva</span>
  <span id="freeText8498360645911077319" style="display:none">My YA recommendation of the month -- which is not really fair since I read the ARC and it doesn't come out until September -- is Jonathan Stroud's Lockwood &amp; Co.: The Screaming Staircase. You may be familiar with Stroud's earlier series about the genie Bartimaeus, and like Bartimaeus, Lockwood &amp; Co. offers us an alternate modern England -- a brilliantly rendered world in which "the Problem" has inexplicably caused ghosts to run rampant and disrupt the lives of mortals. In this new reality, private agencies have arisen to combat the supernatural, and they rely on children as their operatives, since only their senses are keen enough to detect and combat ghosts. After a horrible accident in her home village, Lucy Carlyle flees to London where she joins a small struggling agency, Lockwood &amp; Co., headed by the young and dashing (possibly too reckless) Anthony Lockwood. Soon they are embroiled in a mystery that may cost them their agency and even their lives. Ancient evil, unsolved murders, powerful ghosts and nefarious mortals -- this story will keep you reading late into the night, but you'll want to leave the lights on. Stroud is a genius at inventing an utterly believable world which is very much like ours, but so creepily different. Put The Screaming Staircase on your 'need to read' list when it comes out in September!</span>

<div id="review_2139262534" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2139262534" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2139262534?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552566780" href="/book/show/18657633-the-screaming-staircase">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=fantasy-series">fantasy-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2139262534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8217220794887089512"><i>”Oh, quit complaining. You got naked with a ghost –“</i><br/><br/>Well, if this sentence didn’t capture your immediate attention then I really don’t know! ;-P<br/>It’s one of the many good examples of the amazing humour in this book and I have to admit that this was one of the first things that got me hooked on <b>“Lockwood & Co.”</b>. <br/><br/>The second thing that got me more than just a little curious was the amazing world building though. I just loved the idea of a world that is haunted by ghosts and is in dire need of profes</span>
  <span id="freeText8217220794887089512" style="display:none"><i>”Oh, quit complaining. You got naked with a ghost –“</i><br /><br />Well, if this sentence didn’t capture your immediate attention then I really don’t know! ;-P<br />It’s one of the many good examples of the amazing humour in this book and I have to admit that this was one of the first things that got me hooked on <b>“Lockwood &amp; Co.”</b>. <br /><br />The second thing that got me more than just a little curious was the amazing world building though. I just loved the idea of a world that is haunted by ghosts and is in dire need of professional agencies that get rid of those “Visitors”. I think that’s quite a unique way to introduce a story and the fact that those mentioned professional agents are actually children certainly made everything even more interesting. In this world children are the only ones who are sensitive enough to see, hear or feel a ghosts presence and so the exceptionally gifted are hired as soon as their abilities show. <br /><br /><i>”George can do a bit of that,” the boy said. “Not me. I’m tone-deaf when it comes to Visitors. Sight’s my thing. Death-glows and trails, and all the ghoulish residues of death …” He grinned. “Cheerful subject, isn’t it?”</i><br /><br />Of course Lockwood, Lucy and George are three of those children, even though they already seem to be around 15 or 16 when the book begins. As it seems they started at a young age and will be able to do their job as long as they are no adults. The details are kind of vague here but I hope this will be explained a little more in the following books. XD (Don’t disappoint me, Stroud! *lol*)<br /><br />And if we’re already speaking of the characters: <u>I loved them all!!!</u> Lucy is such an awesome protagonist and you just can’t help but got to love her for her almost reckless badassery! Haha! Yeah, I think that describes her pretty well. XD As for Lockwood? He kind of reminded me of a younger and more cheerful version of Kaz Brekker! *lol* Which is pretty awesome because I love characters that have a brilliant mind! =)) But oh boy, George was so much fun as well!!! <br /><br /><i>”Take his appearance. There was something about it that acted as a trigger to one’s worst instincts. His face was uniquely slappable – a nun would have ached to punch him – while his backside cried out to heaven for a well-placed kick.”</i><br /><br />I really enjoyed Lucy’s and his interactions and gosh, they were so funny! I definitely want to see more of those two! They are really entertaining and what makes it even better is that George isn’t taking Lucy’s accusations and shit! *LOL* He talks back, his comments are scathing and I just live for it! &lt;3 <br /><br />But enough of that, let’s get to their interesting mission! <b>Combe Carey Hall</b>! The haunted house!! <br /><br /><i>”Architecturally it is a peculiar mishmash of a place - passages leading nowhere or doubling back upon themselves, odd changes of level... But more to the point, it has always had a sinister reputation. Stories of Visitors here go back centuries."</i><br /><br />And <b>Fairfax</b> the owner of the aforementioned house!<br /><br /><i>”I must admit, though, I didn’t think he’d have the cheek to rifle through our bags while we weren’t looking. But there you go, that’s a measure of the man he is.”<br />“Why what kind of man is he?” George said, staring at his canister.<br />“A dreadful one. Isn’t it obvious?”</i><br /><br />Sounds intriguing and creepy? You can bet your life on it! It definitely was! (Pun totally intended!! ;-P) Which actually brings me to the last bit of this short review! The intense creepiness of the book! *lol* I mean I admit that I’m a scaredy cat when it comes to horror movies and scary books, but for a supposedly middle grade book this was actually pretty erm… spooky. XD<br />I’m sure I would have loved this book as a kid, but I guess since I’m still a child in my mind my grown up-self had no troubles to enjoy it as well. ;-)<br /><br />All told I really liked <b>“The Screaming Staircase”</b> and I can’t wait to read the next book! <br />Thanks for the attention and now excuse me while I go on an extended shopping trip to buy lavender, salt, iron chains and a few teeny-weeny magnesium flares. <br /><br />Better safe than sorry, right? ;-P</span>
  <a data-text-id="8217220794887089512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1918005041" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15392644487458260164"><b>5 / 5 stars</b><br/><br/><i>MY LOVE FOR THESE THREE IS UNCONDITIONAL IF ANY OF THEM DIE DURNING THIS SERIES I’M DELETING MY GR ACCOUNT AND BECOMING A HERMIT, OKAY? #lucewood</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495363983i/22810157.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book follows Lucy Carlyle, a teenage ghost investigator looking for a job in London during <i>The Problem</i>. The Problem is a ghost infestation, with the dead not staying dead. It resulted in houses being haunted and many dead; and the only people capable of defeating the ghosts are children and teens.<br/><br/>Lucy winds up getting a job at London's m</span>
  <span id="freeText15392644487458260164" style="display:none"><b>5 / 5 stars</b><br><br><i>MY LOVE FOR THESE THREE IS UNCONDITIONAL IF ANY OF THEM DIE DURNING THIS SERIES I’M DELETING MY GR ACCOUNT AND BECOMING A HERMIT, OKAY? #lucewood</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495363983i/22810157.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book follows Lucy Carlyle, a teenage ghost investigator looking for a job in London during <i>The Problem</i>. The Problem is a ghost infestation, with the dead not staying dead. It resulted in houses being haunted and many dead; and the only people capable of defeating the ghosts are children and teens.<br><br>Lucy winds up getting a job at London's more ramshackle agency <i>(much to the disgust of George Cubbins, the deputy of the agency who is in a perpetually bad mood)</i>, where nothing ever works out the way it's supposed to. Bad luck and coincidental accidents follow this agency around like the plague. <br><br>I wouldn't go as far as to say that this trio is better than the famous <b>golden trio</b> <i>(i'm not crazy okay, harry potter can never be bested in my eyes)</i>, but this definitely comes in a close second for me. The way the characters interacted with each other reminded me a lot of HP, and it was the most beautiful thing to find a group of friends who made me just as happy. <br><br>This book was beautiful. It was humorous, suspenseful, and adorable. The characters that filled this novel were nerdy, independent teenagers who had stronger backbones than the adults surrounding them. But hands down, the humour and banter was what made this book brilliant. <br><br><i><blockquote>“Thanks for that,” George said, “I thought they were my best feature”.<br><br>“They are—that’s the tragedy of it.” </blockquote>
<br><br><blockquote>“Lovely summer evening, it was. She stood astride the crenulations, skirt flapping, silhouetted against a blood-red sky, while the servants tried to coax her back in with tea and seed cake. No good, of course.”</blockquote>
<br><br><blockquote>“What?” I said. “Saw what? Nothing happened.”<br><br>“Precisely. Where was HIS slap around the chops? Where was his firm shaking? There’re double standards at work here.”</blockquote> </i><br><br>These are just some of the funniest (and shortest, because I’m too lazy to type out the long funny) passages that literally had me laughing like a crazy person in public—which is <b>not a good look</b>.<br><br>The relationship between Lockwood, George and Lucy filled the majority of the book and I wouldn’t have it any other way. They were a dynamic group of characters, probably some of the best written teenage characters I've ever read about—they weren’t walking stereotypes and they didn’t get on my nerves. <br><br>I’m a sucker for anything English related, and the classic English slang and description just made this all the more atmospheric to me. This is one of those books that must be read late at night with a cup of tea, whilst it’s raining. <br><br>The first quarter was more setting the scene and covering Lucy’s backstory, which was interesting enough, but I didn’t find spectacular. And then I hit about page 150 and I read the rest all in one night. I was the walking dead the next day at work. This is one of those books that feels like only a hundred or so pages because it was so quick to read, the characters were unique, hilarious and realistic—I couldn’t get enough of Lockwood &amp; Co. <br><br>I must admit that I’m not much of a fan of ghost stories, I’m jumpy as hell and oblivious which isn’t a good combination. I am one of those people who gets scared by their own shadow. But in saying this, I found this book creepy, but not scary. The way the world was set up and created was the best part, filled with interesting rules and history that made me fall in love with it.<br><br>The murder mystery didn’t stay much of a mystery for long in my opinion, but it was still extremely interesting to see how all the little details wove together, I cannot wait to see what the next book is about! <br><br><b>GUYS YOU DON’T KNOW HOW SCARED I AM THAT SOMETHING WILL HAPPEN TO LOCKWOOD AND LUCY. MY SHIPPING IS OUT OF HAND ALREADY LOL</b> I need the next book ASAP PLS<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495364096i/22810181.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I just cannot get over Lucy as a character, what a badass. I freaking adore her ugh<br><br><a href="https://art-of-sumi.tumblr.com/image/153134285653" rel="nofollow noopener">[s]</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15392644487458260164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1909459362" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1909459362" />
    <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale"><img alt="Hannah Greendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466436186p2/43377498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1909459362?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah Greendale" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale">Hannah Greendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423186922" href="/book/show/19162620-the-screaming-staircase">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1909459362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11688345036276513892">Lucy Carlyle has two special Talents: she can hear the voices of the dead and she can experience memories of the dead by touching belongings they once owned. Normally she puts her Talent to use for an organization that investigates paranormal phenomena, but when a tragic incident leaves her jobless, she wanders into the office of Lockwood & Co. hoping to find work. There she teams up with Anthony Lockwood and George Cubbins to tackle solving the mystery behind one of the most notoriously haunted</span>
  <span id="freeText11688345036276513892" style="display:none">Lucy Carlyle has two special Talents: she can hear the voices of the dead and she can experience memories of the dead by touching belongings they once owned. Normally she puts her Talent to use for an organization that investigates paranormal phenomena, but when a tragic incident leaves her jobless, she wanders into the office of Lockwood &amp; Co. hoping to find work. There she teams up with Anthony Lockwood and George Cubbins to tackle solving the mystery behind one of the most notoriously haunted houses in London. <br /><br />With much talk of death, murder, and maligned spirits, <i>The Screaming Staircase</i> is worthy of its classification as a middle grade horror novel. Creepy events often arrive with an unnerving suddenness and evoke a satisfying sense of being spooked. Stroud brings numerous eerie settings to life with descriptions of dark hallways, whispered voices, slamming doors, and blood dripping from walls. <br /><br /><i>In fact, it wasn't at all an ugly hallway; in bright sunlight it might have looked quite pleasant. But not so much now, with the last light from the door panes stretching out like skewed coffins on the floor in front of us; and with our shadows neatly framed inside them; and with the manner of old Mr. Hope's death in this very place hanging heavy on our minds.</i> <br /><br />Ever since the Problem - an event that happened decades ago - supernatural beings have wandered the earth, roused by their own accord whenever night falls and reaching the apex of their power at midnight. Stroud's version of a ghost-riddled London is fleshed out and richly imagined with civilians wearing protective charms and herbs wherever they go, an extensive list of paranormal entities on the loose, and commonly known rules for tackling a varied array of supernatural phenomena.<br /><br /><i>When entering a house occupied by a Visitor, it's always best to get in quick. That's one of the first rules you learn. Never hesitate, never linger on the threshold.</i> <br /><br /><i>And there was a switch on the wall, right there. But we didn't attempt to use it. You see, a second rule you learn is this: electricity interferes. It dulls the senses and makes you weak and stupid. It's much better to watch and listen in the dark.</i> <br /><br />Unfortunately, Lucy Carlyle makes for a dull narrator. She has no sparkle. Nothing that makes her special or memorable. She is regularly overshadowed by her gallant associate, Anthony Lockwood. Even dumpy George Cubbins, a gross boy who's the butt of every joke, makes a more amusing addition to the story. <br /><br />Further, <i>The Screaming Staircase</i> is bloated with exposition. At almost four hundred pages, the book tends to drag at times. To be fair, this is the first book in a series, so hopefully the books that follow will require less time to establish backstory. Where the surplus of exposition is occasionally wearisome, the author makes up for it with his carefully crafted sentences: <br /><br /><i>Burning papers, ignited by the first surge from the canister, were plucked aloft, blown directly at my face. I batted them away, watched them whirl off, willed by something unseen. They blew in squalls across the room, landed on books and shelves, on desk and curtains, on curls of wallpaper, on bone-dry files and letters, on dusty cushions on the chair . . . <br />Like stars at dusk, hundreds of little fires winked into being, one after another, high, low, and all around.</i> <br /><br />Finally, a glossary at the back of the book introduces young readers to related terms like <i>ectoplasm</i>, <i>death-glow</i>, <i>ghost-lock</i>, and more. <br /><br />Though it's overstuffed with exposition and reaches a predicable conclusion, <i>The Screaming Staircase</i> is a promising start to a new series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11688345036276513892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1779857139" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1779857139" />
    <a title="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader"><img alt="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579173421p2/43850323.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1779857139?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" href="/user/show/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader">Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423186922" href="/book/show/19162620-the-screaming-staircase">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=not-so-great-but-not-bad-either">not-so-great-but-not-bad-either</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=fantasy-books">fantasy-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=original-and-fresh-story">original-and-fresh-story</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1779857139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1978157603808766280"><b>
  <i><br/>Edit : few months have passed since I read this book and I recently feel I'm missing the characters so I finally made up my mind to buy the second book! Hopefully, I'll buy a copy soon. ☺️<br/></i>
</b><br/><br/><b>THE REVIEW IS POSTED<br/><br/>3.5 Stars.</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>
<br/>"My view is: with you and<br/>George on my team, nothing can stand in our way."<br/>
</blockquote>
  </i>
</b> <br/><br/>The problem has been happening for over 50 years. This problem is an epidemic of supernatural phenomena (ghosts) and there are agencies to help people to deal with their supernatural proble</span>
  <span id="freeText1978157603808766280" style="display:none"><b>
  <i><br>Edit : few months have passed since I read this book and I recently feel I'm missing the characters so I finally made up my mind to buy the second book! Hopefully, I'll buy a copy soon. ☺️<br></i>
</b><br><br><b>THE REVIEW IS POSTED<br><br>3.5 Stars.</b><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>
<br>"My view is: with you and<br>George on my team, nothing can stand in our way."<br>
</blockquote>
  </i>
</b> <br><br>The problem has been happening for over 50 years. This problem is an epidemic of supernatural phenomena (ghosts) and there are agencies to help people to deal with their supernatural problems or the supernatural threat. <br>Lucy Carlyle is a girl who works for an agency called Lockwood &amp; Co. and the leader of this agency is Anthony Lockwood. So they have this one case that doesn't end well and involving fire and because of this they need to pay for the damage and they only have 4 weeks to pay up or it will involve court proceedings and lockwood &amp; Co. can be shut down. So now, they need to save the agency and this problem of theirs leads them to one of the most haunted houses in England. <br><br><b>so you're probably are wondering how much money do they have to pay? and what happens with that case that doesn't end well? and can they save the agency? and will they survive at the end? and what will happen inside the haunted house? <br>well, you have to read the book yourself to know the answers. :p </b><br><br><b>
  <u>My Opinion Time!</u>
</b><br><br>So, it's been a pretty long time since I read a book about ghosts or in the genre of Paranormal. To be honest, Paranormal isn't really my favorite genre but sometimes I still want to read it if it's about ghosts. But if it's about Vampires or Werewolves or fallen angels, etc, I'll just pass. But, it doesn't mean they're not good. it's just that I'm not a fan of them and if you like them, then I totally respect your opinion! :D<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1513438969ra/24690924.gif" width="280" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book has been on my want to read list since last year ( I guess ). But it wasn't my priority so I didn't even remember it (sorry not sorry) and before I read this book, I tried so hard not to have high expectations about it because <b>I WAS SO TIRED OF DISAPPOINTMENT.</b>I still am actually and thank God, this book didn't disappoint me at the end but I'm pretty sure it would disappoint me if I set my expectations high before reading it. <br><br>Most of the time when I read this book, I just felt plain to the plot and the characters. I didn't feel amazed or excited but this book made me curious about how it would end. Seriously, if this book didn't make me curious, I would abandon it and start another book to spend my time. oh and <b>this book didn't scare me at all.</b>Look, I might didn't set my expectations high before reading it but I thought this book would scare me at least. But it didn't. I shouldn't have expected this would happen because <b>I rarely got what I expected</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381033523ra/3909054.gif" width="300" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I honestly don't know whether the problem is within myself or it's the book's fault but the more I think about it, I realize that books rarely scared me and there are two books that actually scared me and I always get confused every time I think about the characters. look, they weren't boring but they weren't fascinating either. They were just ... simple? fine? but thankfully, they were quite funny and I laughed a little bit while reading it.<br><br><b>Overall, I quite enjoyed reading it and it was worth my time and I didn't regret reading at all. I had a quite good time with this book but I would be happier if I enjoyed it more, actually. However, I still don't know whether or not I will continue reading this series. But you'll know when I do. ;D</b><br><br>thank you for reading and liking this review. I appreciate it very much and I hope you all have a great day! ❤❤ <br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><s>
  <b>REVIEW TO COME TOMORROW.</b>
</s><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><b><br>Me : *whispers to the book* <br>Me : <i>Please don't disappoint me. I'm so tired of being disappointed. </i></b></span>

<div id="review_1405073867" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1405073867" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1405073867?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=mystery-thriller-horror">mystery-thriller-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=teacher-time">teacher-time</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1405073867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2574237722884824977"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444067136i/16447973._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Edit 03/25</b> : Reread with my teacher glasses... Well now, this is a success :) Let's see what the kids think now! <br/><br/><b>Why an experiment?</b> To be honest, I wasn't accustomed to discriminating Middle-Grade and Young Adult novels back when I read in French. WHY? This would be because they're similarly advertised (when in hardbacks) - and don't get me started about the New Adult ones which are blended with them : frankly, I applause all the parents who're trying to make some sense of the way books are sold</span>
  <span id="freeText2574237722884824977" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444067136i/16447973._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Edit 03/25</b> : Reread with my teacher glasses... Well now, this is a success :) Let's see what the kids think now! <br><br><b>Why an experiment?</b> To be honest, I wasn't accustomed to discriminating Middle-Grade and Young Adult novels back when I read in French. WHY? This would be because they're similarly advertised (when in hardbacks) - and don't get me started about the New Adult ones which are blended with them : frankly, I applause all the parents who're trying to make some sense of the way books are sold to their teenagers. I mean it. You guys are so brave. <br><br>Anyway, my point is that I stopped reading Middle-Grade novels around the time I started experiencing books in English, running far away each time I saw the "children" shelf. Doing that, 1) I was missing out on some amazing stories, and 2) I couldn't properly recommend books to young teenagers (my older pupils, for example). <br><br>That's why I decided to stop narrowing my possibilities - and here I am, reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13555073.The_Screaming_Staircase__Lockwood___Co____1_" title="The Screaming Staircase (Lockwood &amp; Co., #1) by Jonathan Stroud" rel="nofollow noopener">The Screaming Staircase</a>. <b>No need to say that I don't regret a second of my read.</b><br><br><b><u>Actual rating</u> : 3.5 stars</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444114514i/16455316._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Alternative history is starting to become one of my favorite world-building tropes</b>. How is London different? Basically, the dead decided that to rest in peace was way too boring, and started to wander the earth after dark : first they are many, second they're more dangerous (they have the power to kill you in a blue painful death - yes, it's as horrible as it sounds). <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/33467.Jonathan_Stroud" title="Jonathan Stroud" rel="nofollow noopener">Jonathan Stroud</a>'s trick lies in the fact that only children and teenagers can sense them fully and then, <i>fight</i> them. I really like this idea because this way we don't have to suspend our disbelief about the odds of teenagers investigating, and it constitutes an awesome premise in my opinion.<br><br>Plot wise, what we get here is <b>a murder mystery</b>... <i>Annabel (don't you think this is the most beautiful name of the world? Huh?) was a young socialite in the 60s when she brutally disappeared... until Lockwood and Co find her again during a fucked up mission</i>. <br><br>SPOILER ALERT : She was dead. <br><br><b>This is precisely where the shoe pinches : <u>PREDICTABILITY</u>.</b> Indeed I figured the mystery out pretty fast, and the ending confirmed everything I thought. Is it a fail, then? <br><br>No. <b>I did guess what will happen around 50-60%, but it didn't prevent me from enjoying my read</b>, and to be fair, I still think that it was well-crafted for a MG, way darker and grittier than I would have at first imagined. <br><br>Anyway - despite my tendency to turn into some Nancy Drew, <b>the story was still completely addictive</b>. No need to say more. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444114514i/16455317._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If there's still room for further improvement, for example when it comes to the depth of the characters, <b>I grew attached to them and felt connected</b>, which is not a sure thing in many books. Not to mention that since it's a series, I can completely nurture the hope that they will be (more) developed. <br><br>In a word, if the characterization isn't flawless, the author made me love his characters (all right, with a soft spot for Lockwood) and <b>they're FULL of potential in my opinion</b>. <br><br>First of all, <b>Lucy is a strong female lead, kickass but acknowledging her fears</b>, in other words, my favorite kind. Her inner thoughts gave me several genuine and unexpected laughs (the best kind in my opinion) and I really appreciated the fact that she was never seen as the "weak" member of the team. <br><br>As for <b>George</b>, his nerdness and... hmm... <i>weirdness</i> is smile-inducing, I have to admit. <br><br>And <b>last but not least : Lockwood!</b> God, I love his sarcastic (but never mean) mind and his secretive personality. In my opinion characters are winners when 1)they feel real and 2)they make the readers want to know MORE about them, not because they're one dimensional, but because what we do know is already fascinating. Yet he did annoy me when he started to keep his discoveries and hypothesis to himself : YOU ARE PART OF A TEAM, DUDE. Just don't forget it. Sigh. I'm willing to forgive him, though, but do not do this anymore, okay? <br><br>But most of all <b>I fell in love with the characters' dynamics playing out in the ghosts hunting team</b> : I genuinely think that we have never enough books where friendship is well-portrayed, especially when aiming a younger audience. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444114514i/16455318._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>We need to talk about the scary scenes.</b> Okay. I know what you think. Anna. You're such a pussy. <br><br><i>Annnd</i> you might be right. But. But. But. I didn't imagine the way my heart pounded at some scenes. I'm not delusional. It <i>did</i> happen, and for me, it's everything I need to know when dealing with a ghost story. Did I feel oppressed? YES. WELL DONE. <br><br>Let me get this straight : I wasn't scared TO DEATH, but it did let me... What's the word... <b>Spooky? Jumpy?</b> Now, what you need to know is that I grew up in a house where basically everyone believed in ghosts to a certain extend (not me, though - I'm the cynical of the bunch). My mother most of all. SO, MUM, THIS IS TOTALLY YOUR FAULT.<br><br>Also, in this world when there are ghosts there are spiders as well. Fucking SPIDERS. Will the nightmare never end??? *shivers*<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444114514i/16455319._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>There's no denying that this book is incredibly well-written</b>, and the narration surprisingly GREAT. Really, I am genuinely impressed by the writing and despite being MG, the characters hardly feel more juvenile than YA ones even if they are around 13? 14? 15? (What? I got lost at some point)<br><br>Not to mention that the dialogues made me smile more often than not. <b>Think banter. Sarcasm</b>.<br><br>► <b>All in all, a really good introduction to this series, and I can hardly wait to read the sequel.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444114514i/16455320._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="2574237722884824977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2123495552" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2123495552" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2123495552?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=series-to-complete">series-to-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2123495552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8132838689362603752"><b>well this was totally freaking spooky and scary 👻 </b> Ghost hunting, mansion hauntings, screaming staircases, murder and a trio of best friends? This book really does have it all. All the Good Stuff<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“Of the first few hauntings I investigated with Lockwood & Co. I intend to say little, in part to protect the identity of the victims, in part because of the gruesome nature of the incidents, but mainly because, in a variety of ingenious ways, we succeeded in messing them all up.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>I'm shocked you peo</span>
  <span id="freeText8132838689362603752" style="display:none"><b>well this was totally freaking spooky and scary 👻 </b> Ghost hunting, mansion hauntings, screaming staircases, murder and a trio of best friends? This book really does have it all. All the Good Stuff<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“Of the first few hauntings I investigated with Lockwood &amp; Co. I intend to say little, in part to protect the identity of the victims, in part because of the gruesome nature of the incidents, but mainly because, in a variety of ingenious ways, we succeeded in messing them all up.” </blockquote>
</i><br><br>I'm shocked you people all read this as children because <i>some parts of this are genuinely terrifying</i>. Don't know if it was the book itself, or the spooky voices the author put on to voice the ghosts, but I, for one, had the chills. <br><br>The Screaming Staircase is the first book in a ghost hunting series - we're introduced to The Problem, an invasion of ghosts and other ghoulies in London. Enter: The Agencies, companies run by adults that use children to investigate hauntings. Only children can sense ghosts and our protagonist Lucy Carlyle is particularly susceptible to hearing their voices. When she joins Lockwood &amp; Co, the only independent Agency run by children in London, she has to help her new friends and colleagues Anthony Lockwood and George Cubbins investigate not only the murder of a young woman, but also the most haunted building in London. Their reputation as an agency is on the line, and so are their lives. <br><br>This book had so many elements I love, just in general but especially in middle grade. Strong friendships between the main characters, hilarious banter, and plenty of action. I listened to the whole middle of this book in one day because I was so drawn in by the action. <br><br>I think what I loved most though was the agency given to the children. Especially since this is middle grade, the focus on the children being capable and talented and not needing adults to interfere was my favourite. The focus on the plight of the children and how they were exploited by their agencies was one of my favourite themes of this book, and it's especially important considering this is middle grade. <br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1512620313i/24620433._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br>But I definitely think what was most memorable about this book was the characters. Lucy, George and Anthony are such fun protagonists to follow, and kind of reminded me of the Golden Trio. Each had a very unique voice and characteristics, and they were also quite fleshed out. Lucy especially was a fun female protagonist for me, she was so quick witted and talented!<br><br>Finally, the world building was very well done. Without being cumbersome the world was explained and there was so much interesting backstory and history, like the legendary Fitz's, or the development of the agencies, and how The Problem started at all. I think the worldbuilding was very detailed and complex, and managed to be so without feeling like it was all being dumped on me. Very well done. <br><br>Since I listened on audio, I should mention the narrator of the audiobook did an AWESOME job. The voices she used for each character were unique and easy to follow, plus the ghost voices were so spooky. I think she definitely managed to make it atmospheric and it was very easy to visualise which I liked. <br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1512620313i/24620432._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br>I will definitely continue this series, though I kinda wanna read one in physical form to see how everything is freakin spelt haha. But this series is definitely as fun and action packed as everyone said! The characters are great and I really want to follow their development and growth as a team, and to see those dynamics change and develop. Plus, the Anthony/Lucy ship must rise ?? This book just set up the whole series really nicely and I'm sure the books will get better and better<br><br>If you're looking for something a bit spooky with good worldbuilding, lots of action and characters who will actually make you laugh out loud go no further !</span>
  <a data-text-id="8132838689362603752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7835613793928608509"><b>4.25 Golden Stars</b><br/><br/>wow! the Winchesters definitely need some iron swords too! (but I mostly preferred Iron rings to punch the ghosts in the face!)   <span id="freeText7835613793928608509" style="display:none"><b>4.25 Golden Stars</b><br /><br />wow! the Winchesters definitely need some iron swords too! (but I mostly preferred Iron rings to punch the ghosts in the face!) XD<br /><br />okay, out of Supernatral tv shows, into Lockwood &amp; Co:<br /><br /><i>about the Concept:</i><br /><br />if you like supernatural horror detective stories, you probably like this.<br />if you are in Winchester brothers fanclub, you like this.<br />if you watch (&amp; like/love) Supernatural TV shows, you definitely like this.<br /><br />tho at first two pages, I had Sherlock vibes, but in general, I felt I was in a #SPN investigation (I was constantly screaming internally <i>'get the salt!', 'burn the bones!', 'Ahhhh, Getting Cold! Be careful!'</i> during reading it. &amp; it was exhilarating, fun &amp; amazing!<br /><br />One thing is clear, it's not a mere middle grade (as I just see it categorized as middle grade); a.k.a it's an amazing, worth reading middle grade or in other words, it's regardless of age middle grade.<br /><br />supernatural, mild horror, thrilling, exciting, low fantasy, fun story!<br />it was one of the most anticipated books I wanted to read &amp; I really enjoy reading this.<br />it was a quick read.<br /><br />I loved Lockwood! He was good, confident &amp; funny leader. (with messy black hair; coincidence? (that I love him) I don't think so!)<br />Lucy wasn't annoying, but not added to my fav heroines too. (yet?)<br />&amp; although the writing style was 1st person view of a girl, but I didn't get annoyed at all! &amp; that's awesome!<br />-<br />World building: ★★★★/5<br />Characters: ★★★★/5<br />Written style: ★★★★/5<br />plot &amp; events: ★★★★/5<br />General idea: ★★★★★/5</span>

<div id="review_1918145741" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1918145741" />
    <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net"><img alt="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390032p2/7971097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1918145741?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net">Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1918145741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4241906917328130573"><i>See this review and more like it on <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.bookbastion.net'>www.bookbastion.net</a>!</i><br/>_________<br/><br/>Well that was fun and basically everything I hoped it would be! <br/><br/>Every once in awhile, in the midst of all my fantasy and YA reads I get a craving to read something just a little bit <i>spooky</i>. When I first came across some friends on my feed raving about this book, it immediately called to me. <b>What's spookier than ghosts? To me, not much! </b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461106225ra/18825176.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I wasn't sure when I could fit this into my reading schedule until Netgalley emailed me a widget </span>
  <span id="freeText4241906917328130573" style="display:none"><i>See this review and more like it on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookbastion.net">www.bookbastion.net</a>!</i><br>_________<br><br>Well that was fun and basically everything I hoped it would be! <br><br>Every once in awhile, in the midst of all my fantasy and YA reads I get a craving to read something just a little bit <i>spooky</i>. When I first came across some friends on my feed raving about this book, it immediately called to me. <b>What's spookier than ghosts? To me, not much! </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461106225ra/18825176.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I wasn't sure when I could fit this into my reading schedule until Netgalley emailed me a widget for the first book, at which point I couldn't pass it up. <br><br>There was a lot to love here. For starters, <b>I love the whole alternate history idea: a world where ghosts have been proven to exist, and they're actually incredibly dangerous to the living.</b> A world where children's latent psychic abilities turn them into weapons against the dead. At first glance there's a lot to learn as Stroud has filled the book with terms unique to this world he's created. Thankfully, there's a glossary at the back of the book, so no one need get too lost while reading. There's also a lot of backstory provided that help to establish the world and all these ghostly aspects of it for the reader. <br><br>The way these components of the story are introduced are a bit overwhelming, but <b>I prefer the way this book avoids infodumping by just getting on with the story and hoping the reader catches on over time.</b> It's a bit like being thrown into the deep end but also being provided with swimming lessons along the way to ensure you don't drown in the details. <br><br><b>Stroud manages to balance the spooky with the silly quite well here.</b> The ghosts are definitely scary, but the dialogue and interactions between the living characters provide a necessary levity to the events, so children who read the book won't be too scared out of their wits. Like a new age Beetlejuice, there's a levity here that was unexpected but also quite welcome. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446769250ra/16894148.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>The three leads have such great chemistry together.</b> I got an extreme Doctor Who vibe from Lockwood especially. As the leader of their little paranormal investigative outfit, and typically the most informed about the paranormal, Lockwood felt very Doctor-ish to me, and Lucy and George, his companions/assistants. Basically, I was imaging this the entire way through: <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504972471ra/23854836.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The characters provided the necessary dynamic for a lot of Lockwood's revelations and intellect about their investigations to shine through. Now, I'm a big fan of all things Doctor Who, so finding such similarity in the way these characters are built was quite a pleasant surprise to me. <br><br><b>The only reason I'm detracting a star is because I thought the plotting could have been a bit tighter.</b> The story is broken up into 5 parts, "The Ghost; Before; The Necklace; The Hall; And After," a decision that thought felt a bit wonky. I spent nearly 50% of the book trying to figure out what the main plot of the book was actually going to be about. All of the events and the ghostly encounters are certainly a great deal of fun, but I think I would have enjoyed it a tiny bit more had there been a clearer plot arc to the story. <br><br>It might just be a case of the first book in a series needing to spend so much time establishing the world and aspects of it that the plot got a little sidelined. <b>I'm hopeful that the next books in the series will have a clearer focus on direct plot movement now that the world has been properly introduced.</b> Regardless, the events in this story are certainly entertaining and they fulfilled that need for a spooky read I was looking for, so I had a great time reading. <br><br>Looking forward to reading the next books soon! <br><br><b>4 out of 5 stars!</b><br>_________<br><br><i>Thank you Netgalley and Disney-Hyperion for the opportunity to read and review this book!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4241906917328130573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1944732413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14433205738798059078"><b> 3 Stars<br/><br/>Overview: </b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494384996ra/22709750.gif' width='400' height='210' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>^ Basically my entire feelings about this book. I can appreciate it, but something about it didn’t click. I just don’t think it was for me. <br/><br/>I <i>liked it</i>. I just didn’t love it. <br/><br/>Buddy Read with the lovely <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/61971658-frankie-westfall' rel='nofollow noopener'>Frankie!</a> Who enjoyed this much more than I did!<br/><br/><b> Pros: </b><br/><br/>There’s some <i>super</i> cool worldbuilding. It’s ghosts mixed with science and somehow <i>it works.</i> This is set in a London where the world is almost over-run with paranormal activity, and children are the only ones able to detect the</span>
  <span id="freeText14433205738798059078" style="display:none"><b> 3 Stars<br><br>Overview: </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494384996ra/22709750.gif" width="400" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>^ Basically my entire feelings about this book. I can appreciate it, but something about it didn’t click. I just don’t think it was for me. <br><br>I <i>liked it</i>. I just didn’t love it. <br><br>Buddy Read with the lovely <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/61971658-frankie-westfall" rel="nofollow noopener">Frankie!</a> Who enjoyed this much more than I did!<br><br><b> Pros: </b><br><br>There’s some <i>super</i> cool worldbuilding. It’s ghosts mixed with science and somehow <i>it works.</i> This is set in a London where the world is almost over-run with paranormal activity, and children are the only ones able to detect them. It's a fun premise that's carried out well. <br><br>The atmosphere is deliciously creepy and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/33467.Jonathan_Stroud" title="Jonathan Stroud" rel="nofollow noopener">Jonathan Stroud</a> brilliantly uses sensory details to illustrate a scene. Definitely spookier than I expected, and even my hyper-rational brain was wincing at shadows after some late-night-reading.<br><br>Lockwood is a delightfully cocky lil thing without being calloused or uncaring. This was well-balanced combo that I really appreciated. <br><br>There’s some really witty and hilarious dialogue that I really enjoyed. <br><br><b> Cons </b><br><br>It was glaringly obvious to me that I was outside the target age. I don’t think I’ve ever felt more old until I was half-way through thinking, “You’re how old again? Why don’t you spend your money wisely? How come none of you have guardians or parental supervison at all? Why is everyone so reckless?”<br><br>There’s just a lot of middle-grade humor and I think my inner-child is on vacation or something, but it just didn’t work for me. Like I get it. George in his underwear is supposed to be funny. <br><br>Lucy, our narrator, was <i>so</i> boring. She stands up for herself and has ideas… but that’s kind of it? It felt like she didn’t have a ton of personality and her voice was overall really dry. I spent the first third of this convinced it was a historical because the way she speaks is so… wordy? Outdated? It just felt very off and bored me. <br><br><s>I’m actually still not completely certain this isn’t a historical. I’m sorry if it is. </s><br><br><b> In Conclusion </b><br><br> A creepy adventure with a fun cast of characters—that I’m sure others more used to Middle Grade will enjoy more than I did. <br><br>(Also I'm sorry <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/26402455-sana-khalid" rel="nofollow noopener">Sana.<br> </a> <s>At least I didn't DNF and one star it.</s>)</span>

  <span id="freeText6965763090115159925" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"Okay," I hurried on. "But why me?" <br>"You're a girl," Lockwood called. "Aren't you supposed to be more sensitive?" <br>"To emotions, yes. To nuances of human behavior. Not necessarily to secret passages in a wall." <br>"Oh, it's much the same thing."</i>

<div id="review_1832778594" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1832778594" />
    <a title="Frankie Lovely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61971658-frankie-lovely"><img alt="Frankie Lovely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493240668p2/61971658.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1832778594?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Frankie Lovely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Frankie Lovely" href="/user/show/61971658-frankie-lovely">Frankie Lovely</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Frankie Lovely by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/26402455-sana">Sana</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61971658-frankie-lovely?shelf=read-it-in-2017">read-it-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61971658-frankie-lovely?shelf=rtc-review-to-come">rtc-review-to-come</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61971658-frankie-lovely?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61971658-frankie-lovely?shelf=rtc-rating-to-come">rtc-rating-to-come</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61971658-frankie-lovely?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61971658-frankie-lovely?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61971658-frankie-lovely?shelf=want-to-own">want-to-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61971658-frankie-lovely?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1832778594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3125460982015610382"><b>4.5 stars<br/>See this review and others at <a href='https://athousandlivesoffrankielovely.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Thousand Lives of Frankie Lovely</a><br/>Buddy read with my girl <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/47627265-kaylin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kaylin</a></b> who did not love this as much as I did.<br/><br/>Ok so … I LOVED it<br/>Also, my inner child has a new book boyfriend<br/><br/><b>The Story</b><br/><br/>Perhaps better titled “The world”, because I am going to avoid telling you anything about the actual story. Some things are better left to your own discovery and I feel like this book is one of those instances.<br/><br/>Lucy can hear things … not the things you and I can hear (for we - at least</span>
  <span id="freeText3125460982015610382" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars<br />See this review and others at <a href="https://athousandlivesoffrankielovely.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">A Thousand Lives of Frankie Lovely</a><br />Buddy read with my girl <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/47627265-kaylin" rel="nofollow noopener">Kaylin</a></b> who did not love this as much as I did.<br /><br />Ok so … I LOVED it<br />Also, my inner child has a new book boyfriend<br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br /><br />Perhaps better titled “The world”, because I am going to avoid telling you anything about the actual story. Some things are better left to your own discovery and I feel like this book is one of those instances.<br /><br />Lucy can hear things … not the things you and I can hear (for we - at least most of us - are much too old). No. Lucy Carlyle can hear paranormal activity. Ghosts and apparitions and the things that go bump in the night. <br /><br />It has been over 50 years since the beginning of “the problem”, that is, the arrival of a devastating ghost epidemic that is terrorizing the city of London. Dangerous things lurk in the night, and the ones who can stop these hauntings … the agents … or Psychic Investigation Agencies. Typically, such agencies are managed by adults (though adults lack the gifts needed to fight “the problem”) while the agents consist of talented children with certain abilities. However, Lockwood &amp; Co. is different in every way. Lockwood &amp; Co. is owned and operated solely by children and is the smallest - and perhaps not what one might call the most prestigious - agency in London ... and the talented Lucy Carlyle is about to find herself a member of this crew of three.<br /><br /><b>What I liked</b><br /><br />This book was so much fun! I haven't really given middle grade books enough of a chance in my reading routine and this really needs to be remedied. To be honest, I have read way too many YA and even adult books that were not this well written or developed. There is a certain stigma to middle grade books, that somehow this book will not relate to me or be interesting to me because I am “past that point” in my life (which is a dumb way for me to think, considering that YA is my favorite genre and I am certainly beyond that point in my life as well). This book was not childish in any way. It was dark and twisted while also maintaining a lightness that was refreshing and had me laughing out loud. It also made me afraid of the dark (which let’s face it is not a difficult feat as I am pretty much terrified of anything relating to spiritual and ghost activity … yeah I'm a wuss). I guess what I'm getting at here is that, while this is middle grade, it is for an older middle grade audience and very easily appeals to an even wider audience still.<br /><br />The writing of these books is fantastic. Again, as I stated above, I have read many many many YA and adult books that were not this well written and developed. The world is an easy to understand and unique world, the characters are complex and really well developed, the subject matter is appealing to a large audience, and basically I am well on my way to being Lockwood trash.<br /><br />So let’s talk for a minute about the characters, because these kids are the best thing about this series (not to take away from the fact that everything about this series is also pretty awesome). Ok so, yes. My inner child is in love with Anthony Lockwood! I will shout it from the rooftops. He is a precious child and I love him dearly. Lockwood’s character, as you will see, is very secretive. It is obvious that he has many ghosts in his closet (no pun intended), but he is also very lighthearted. I do adore a broken character and I get the feeling that Lockwood is hiding some pain behind his bluster and snark. But oh the snark! I love it so so so much I can't stand it! Lockwood’s sarcastic attitude is everything I need to give this book the lightness that it needs to counter balance the sometimes gruesome and heavy themes of the stories. Speaking of snark and lighthearted banter, I would be remiss not to mention the other shining star of this series! George Cubbins. Oh my sweet little nerdy naïve child! George is the researcher of the crew and is sometimes a bit too literal - which makes for some fun banter and funny moments. He is also pretty snarky which, have I mentioned I love snark? In some ways, I actually enjoyed his character more than Lockwood. George has a certain humor that is dry and witty and aloof that meshes perfectly with my own personal brand of funny. He is dedicated (overly so at times) to his research and experiments, again lending to some pretty funny moments. And basically the only time I liked our third and final main character (and narrator) Lucy, was during her interactions (aka arguments) with George. Which brings me, of course, to the tiny little blip of negatives I had with this book.<br /><br /><b>What I did not like</b><br /><br />Unfortunately, I did find Lucy (our narrator) to be a little bit on the boring side. Her character is just as developed as the others, but she is simply a more reserved character overall. I would not call her weak or timid though. She has some interesting backstory in this book which I enjoyed, and as mentioned above, some really great banter with both Lockwood and George. But there was just something about her point of view that I found the slightest bit lacking at times (but only in small measure). Because of this, and because of the slowish pacing of certain parts of the story, this book took me a little bit to get into. But once I was in … I was all in!<br /><br /><b>In conclusion</b><br /><br />I loved this book and these characters and this world and this idea and the mixing of light humor with dark subjects. This book is fantastic and I cannot wait to read more in the series! I'm going to say it now … I see the possibility for a full fledged obsession forming and I couldn't be more happy about it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3125460982015610382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously"><img alt="Rachel Reads Ravenously" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539149211p2/14514998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2300806607?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423186922" href="/book/show/19162620-the-screaming-staircase">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=reread">reread</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2300806607" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2881985151839834400"><b> Audio re-read August 2019.<br/>Thoughts remain the same! </b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513367806i/24684994._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b> 4 stars! </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “Of the first few hauntings I investigated with Lockwood & Co. I intend to say little, in part to protect the identity of the victims, in part because of the gruesome nature of the incidents, but mainly because, in a variety of ingenious ways, we succeeded in messing them all up.”</i> </b><br/><br/>Who knew a middle grade novel could be TERRIFYING! It took me a while to get through this book because I was too scared to read it at night!<br/><br/>The Screaming</span>
  <span id="freeText2881985151839834400" style="display:none"><b> Audio re-read August 2019.<br>Thoughts remain the same! </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513367806i/24684994._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> 4 stars! </b><br><br><b> <i> “Of the first few hauntings I investigated with Lockwood &amp; Co. I intend to say little, in part to protect the identity of the victims, in part because of the gruesome nature of the incidents, but mainly because, in a variety of ingenious ways, we succeeded in messing them all up.”</i> </b><br><br>Who knew a middle grade novel could be TERRIFYING! It took me a while to get through this book because I was too scared to read it at night!<br><br>The Screaming Staircase takes place in England, where an epidemic of ghosts has covered the country with people taking extra precautions to keep them away. Since younger people have better abilities to see and sense them, they are the front of the army against this supernatural issue.<br><br>Lucy has the gift of hearing ghosts and is excellent at what she does. She joins the Lockwood and Company, a small ghost hunting agency run by Anthony Lockwood with another boy named George. The three of them work to rid the world of ghosts, one haunting at a time…. <br><br><b> <i> “Really?"<br>"No. I'm being ironic. Or is it sarcastic? I can never remember."<br>"Irony's cleverer, so you're probably being sarcastic.” </i> </b><br><br>I’ve had several people recommend me this book and I’ve always meant to get to it. I am very glad I finally did and tried a new to me author, because this book is excellent. It’s like Supernatural for tweens, but in England and with a female lead character. I love the concept of younger adults being placed into adult situations because they are the only ones who can help.<br><br>As I mentioned before, this book was fairly scary. So much so that after finishing it I needed to watch rom coms to get me out of my frightened glow. Stroud is a compelling and excellent writer and I am definitely going to be reading the other books in this series soon. <br><br><b> <i> “Well, when you're being held at gunpoint by a geriatric madman in a metal skirt, you've kind of hit rock bottom anyway. It can't really get much worse.” </i> </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1494101706i/22685352._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Follow me on ♥ <a href="http://www.facebook.com/rachelreadsravenously" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> ♥ <a href="http://rachelsreadsravenously.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> ♥ <a href="http://instagram.com/rachelreadsravenously" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ♥ <a href="https://twitter.com/rayliz89" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ♥</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3579385665?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>,
