        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3579385665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9713563493225072236">I feel different when I read stories that involve ghosts than when I read stories that involve other supernatural or paranormal beings. <br/><br/>I guess it’s because I actually do believe in ghosts and spirits, whereas I don’t, for example, believe in vampires, werewolves, witches (although I’d love to be able to say that I do) or fairies. <br/><br/>It’s not like I believe the world Jonathan Stroud created could one day become OUR world, so I can read this with interest in the topic but also detached from it. Beca</span>
  <span id="freeText9713563493225072236" style="display:none">I feel different when I read stories that involve ghosts than when I read stories that involve other supernatural or paranormal beings. <br /><br />I guess it’s because I actually do believe in ghosts and spirits, whereas I don’t, for example, believe in vampires, werewolves, witches (although I’d love to be able to say that I do) or fairies. <br /><br />It’s not like I believe the world Jonathan Stroud created could one day become OUR world, so I can read this with interest in the topic but also detached from it. Because, really, I don’t think one day our society will be infested with ghosts and that we will have prominent ghostbusting agencies. <br /><br />But then again I didn’t think we’d one day be in confinement due to a pandemic, so who knows. Maybe Jonathan Stroud knows something we don’t. I’d better get ahead and learn everything I can about this subject. <br /><br />So this book. It’s good, it’s really good. The mystery is well done, meaning that I didn’t see most things coming, and I found this character trio, which comprises Lucy, Lockwood and George, pretty entertaining. The first 80 pages were basically unnecessary but the story picked up very quickly after and I did not want to let go! There’s no way I’m not picking the second book up soon. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a>Youtube</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11520853872553124868">This YA spooky series was a surprise for me! I enjoyed the book more than I thought I would.<br/>The writing was well done, the plot was complex and the scary moments were fantastic. I really enjoyed the world building that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/33467.Jonathan_Stroud' title='Jonathan Stroud' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jonathan Stroud</a> has produced with the hauntings, how to destroy them and the type of world the characters live in because of this ghostly issue, aka "The Problem".<br/><br/>The Problem is the epidemic of hauntings currently affecting Britain and how only young children and teenagers can act</span>
  <span id="freeText11520853872553124868" style="display:none">This YA spooky series was a surprise for me! I enjoyed the book more than I thought I would.<br />The writing was well done, the plot was complex and the scary moments were fantastic. I really enjoyed the world building that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/33467.Jonathan_Stroud" title="Jonathan Stroud" rel="nofollow noopener">Jonathan Stroud</a> has produced with the hauntings, how to destroy them and the type of world the characters live in because of this ghostly issue, aka "The Problem".<br /><br />The Problem is the epidemic of hauntings currently affecting Britain and how only young children and teenagers can actually see the ghosts. So they are put into work at an early age to destroy the phantoms, poltergeist and other baddies.<br /><br />I also enjoyed the characters of Lockwood &amp; Co; Anthony, Lucy and George more then expected.<br />I had a few issues with their age in the beginning of the book but I always struggle when characters do stupid and impulsive acts. But then 1/2 way through the book, the characters become less impulsive and this worked for me. Yay!<br /><br />If you like YA series, I think you will love these books and if you like spooky books, the same.<br />I'm super picky with YA series but this worked for me.<br />One other thing that I liked, no instalove or a love relationship with teenagers in this book. Woohoo!<br /><br />I'm actually looking forward to reading the rest of the books in this series!</span>

<div id="review_716149722" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/716149722" />
    <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata"><img alt="Faye, la Patata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557835753p2/7650833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/716149722?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye, la Patata" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata">Faye, la Patata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=1st-in-series">1st-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=fun-narration">fun-narration</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=haunting-narration">haunting-narration</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=good-hero">good-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=good-heroine">good-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer716149722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3111307416435014814"><a href='http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238998i/681660._SX540_.png' height='120' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>Man, this book was awesome and impressive.</b> To be honest, although there are a lot of good MG stuff out there, I'm still a bit wary of this demographic because there is a fair amount of books out there in this category that is absolutely juvenile. But <i>The Screaming Staircase</i> screamed unique, it screamed different, it screamed <b>FANTASTIQUE!</b> in big, bold letters. There is so much to love in this book: the endearing, well-polished characters; the enchanting, well-written narration; and the hypnot</span>
  <span id="freeText3111307416435014814" style="display:none"><a href="http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238998i/681660._SX540_.png" height="120" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Man, this book was awesome and impressive.</b> To be honest, although there are a lot of good MG stuff out there, I'm still a bit wary of this demographic because there is a fair amount of books out there in this category that is absolutely juvenile. But <i>The Screaming Staircase</i> screamed unique, it screamed different, it screamed <b>FANTASTIQUE!</b> in big, bold letters. There is so much to love in this book: the endearing, well-polished characters; the enchanting, well-written narration; and the hypnotic, effective atmosphere. LOVE LOVE LOVE!<br><br><b>One thing you should know about me is that I love a good scare. I relish the feeling of getting creeped out as it's one of those sensations that make me feel so alive.</b> When I'm with friends and we're having sleepovers, I love sharing ghost stories with them, to the point that I suggest we go out ghost-hunting in supposedly haunted places (which was never realized, by the way... in the end, we become wussies) and sometimes, I even have the audacity to encourage using an ouija board to communicate with otherwordly beings (also never realized... the chances of it backfiring are rather high!). Long story short, I <b>love</b> horror. From movies to real life experiences, I've seen them all. But for some reason, books with ghosts never made me feel as scared. Most often than not, the horror factor in these books is utterly laughable, and I find myself disappointed over and over again. <br><br>But goodness, <i>The Screaming Staircase</i> totally changed all that. <b>I can sincerely say this is better written than a lot of Young Adult novels out there.</b><br><br>The world is plagued with ghosts, ever since The Problem started, and the government has been using kids to find and exterminate them. Why kids? Because since their senses are still developing, they are more sensitive to these kinds of things. One of these agencies is Lockwood and Co., and independent organization (meaning free of adult supervision) run by three people - Anthony Lockwood, George Cubbins, and Lucy Carlyle. Together, they run into a lot of obstacles and a lot of mysteries, some of them possibly changing their lives forever.<br><br><b>For a Middle Grade book, this is dark, gritty, and quite violent.</b> I was honestly expecting something a bit more mellow and gentle, maybe a simple ghostly apparition of a harmless ghost, but damn, the ghosts here are not just fucking scary but they are dangerous, too. There are different types, and the most dangerous ones can change their appearances and can kill. They can touch you and the area touched will rot. Of course, a lot of the ghosts ARE harmless, but there are a number of them, those who died violently and whose energies are still contained in certain objects, who can really make you think twice about engaging them.<b> I loved how it gave me that violent sense of urgency and suspense, how it made me want to hide under the covers, and how it actually made me open my lights before sleeping.</b><br><br><b>I guess the writing is a factor of that, too, considering how it was so effective in giving the book a spooky atmosphere. Sure, there are instances where it's light-hearted and fun, but in the scenes that matter the most, it has done an excellent job of immersing you in the story and making you feel you are with the characters as they explore the haunted places. </b>The description of the surroundings, the description of the feelings they feel when they sense a dangerous entity is near, the internal narration of the main character, Lucy... all of it were absolutely <b>BRILLIANT</b>. I cannot stress this enough. I've read a lot of horror in my time, but none of them EVER made the mood right, at least, not as effective as Stroud has done. <br><br><b>The characters were fun to read as well.</b> Lockwood was adventurous, brave, reckless, and calm; George was sarcastic, cynical, intelligent, and cautious; Lucy was endearing, talented, and emotional. They're all so different in many ways, but together as a group, they were amazing and blended beautifully. It was fun to see them banter, protect each other, sort out the puzzles, etc. etc. <b>Just for their dynamics and interaction alone, this book's already worth it.</b><br><br>Honestly, I have troubles deciding which is this book's strongest asset - the narration, the characters, or the mood/atmosphere? All of them were absolutely well done and written that's it's hard to pick. It's <b>that</b> amazing. I absolutely recommend this to everyone, especially those who want to give themselves a good scare or want to read something unique, fun, and dark at the same time.<br><br><b>No doubt a perfect 5 over 5!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3111307416435014814" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12549340915779954505">I mostly requested this because I'd heard good things about it, and boy am I glad I did. This book is awesome!<br/><br/>I think that this is a children's book (middle grade maybe?) but don't let that put you off. This book is ridiculously well written, reading with the flair and complexity of only the best books (ever) and I freaking loved it.<br/><br/>This book is creepy and a little bit scary, set in a terrifying alternate world where ghosts have taken over the night and have the power to kill. When only the youn</span>
  <span id="freeText12549340915779954505" style="display:none">I mostly requested this because I'd heard good things about it, and boy am I glad I did. This book is awesome!<br /><br />I think that this is a children's book (middle grade maybe?) but don't let that put you off. This book is ridiculously well written, reading with the flair and complexity of only the best books (ever) and I freaking loved it.<br /><br />This book is creepy and a little bit scary, set in a terrifying alternate world where ghosts have taken over the night and have the power to kill. When only the young can help to fight this threat, you can kiss goodbye to being a child. Children grow up too fast, too young, and risk their lives to protect everyone else.<br /><br />The characters are marvellous. Each of them is individually strong, but as a team they are totally kick-ass.<br /><br />Lucy is a refreshingly strong female lead who can stand on her own two feet. Despite her flaws she's no damsel in distress. She even saves the boys!<br /><br />Both of the boys are complex too, with flaws of their own. Lockwood is infuriatingly mysterious and secretive - no one knows his background. But saying that, we don't know much about George either.<br /><br />There is so much to learn, so much that I want to know, that I can't wait to read the next one.<br /><br />This book is wonderfully written, set in a spine-tinglingly chilling world with a cast of crazy-marvellous, strong characters. It made me want to curl up in a nest of pillows and cushions and blankets and drink hot tea and eat jam sandwiches.<br /><br />Simply? This book is marvellous.<br /><br /><b>ETA</b><br />This is one of those books that I push on people. A lot. Family? Check. Friends? Check. Random people in a book shop? Check. EVERYONE EVER? Check.<br /><br /><i>I received a copy of this for free via NetGalley for review purposes.</i></span>

<div id="review_1076009211" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1076009211" />
    <a title="Madeline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111921-madeline"><img alt="Madeline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1220803522p2/111921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1076009211?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madeline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madeline" href="/user/show/111921-madeline">Madeline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=kids-and-young-adult">kids-and-young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1076009211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17093324436089068407">I can't believe I almost forgot about Jonathan Stroud. His Bartimaeus trilogy was one of my favorites when I was in middle school/high school, but I never thought I would find another one of his books, because for some reason I believed that he hadn't written anything else after that series. It was pure chance that I learned about this book at all - I can't remember which of my Goodreads friends put this on their to-read list, but someone did, and I happened to be looking at my feed at the exact</span>
  <span id="freeText17093324436089068407" style="display:none">I can't believe I almost forgot about Jonathan Stroud. His Bartimaeus trilogy was one of my favorites when I was in middle school/high school, but I never thought I would find another one of his books, because for some reason I believed that he hadn't written anything else after that series. It was pure chance that I learned about this book at all - I can't remember which of my Goodreads friends put this on their to-read list, but someone did, and I happened to be looking at my feed at the exact right moment, so whoever it was, I thank you. It's been at least ten years since I read the Bartimaeus books, and going back to Stroud's writing was like catching up with an old friend. <br /><br />Like his previous series, <i>The Screaming Staircase</i> concerns supernatural elements and takes place in Stroud's signature setting, London in an unspecified time period that feels like it should be the Victorian era but isn't (seriously, I don't know how Stroud does it - there's never anything in his books that specifically says "we're in the reign of Queen Victoria right now," but somehow that's always how I imagine the setting, and then I'm totally thrown off whenever someone starts talking about plastic or microwaves). With the Bartimaeus trilogy, it was demons and magicians. Here, it's ghosts. <br /><br />The book starts out <i>in media res</i>, with teenagers Lucy Carlyle and Anthony Lockwood going to ghost-bust a haunted house. This is a great way to open the story, because we get to see Lucy and Lockwood in action and learn about their specific ghost-hunting gifts (Lockwood can see death-glows, and Lucy is an empath who can hear spirits and their emotions) without needing to sit through lots of buildup and exposition. It's only after the ghost-hunting section is over, and we're fully hooked, that Stroud has Lucy explain what's going on to the reader. About fifty years ago, she tells us, England was beset by "the Problem." Ghosts started appearing every night, and worse, they gained the ability to hurt people - Lucy talks about "ghost-touch," which can kill a person. Ghosts are invisible to adults, but children can see them, and have psychic abilities that fade when they grow up. So now ghost-hunting has become a profession in England, and the ghost hunters are all children and teenagers (which is a very neat solution to the central problem found in most YA-adventure lit, the question of why children are always running around unsupervised with weapons and magic). The worldbuilding is fantastic, with Stroud fully exploring what a society threatened by ghosts would look like. City-wide curfews are enforced, because ghosts only come out at night, and houses have to be protected with iron and channels of running water to keep the ghosts out. As I said, ghost-hunting has become an official profession, and Lucy works for Lockwood &amp; Co, a pretty ragtag agency consisting of her, Lockwood, and another boy named George (who has been rather unfairly left off the cover of every edition of this book). <br /><br />The job that's described in the beginning of the book is what starts the action. Lucy and Lockwood discover the body of a girl who was murdered fifty years ago (and is therefore the source of the haunting). The murderer was never caught, so the group starts trying to figure out who killed the girl, while also trying to keep their agency from going bankrupt. Then they get hired to investigate one of the most haunted buildings in England - it houses the screaming staircase of the title, and also "the Red Room" and don't worry, it's just as terrifying as it sounds. <br /><br />The writing is sharp and witty, although none of the kids can match Bartimaeus in snark. All of the ghosts are legitimately terrifying, and the entire sequence at the haunted house is suspenseful and delightfully scary. The characters are well-done and fun, and Lucy is a fantastic heroine. <br /><br />This was the only wobbly part of an otherwise well-paced, witty, scary, and well-written story - the haunted house and the murder investigation seem like two separate stories, and don't really mesh well together even after we learn how they're connected. The murder mystery itself is pretty good, but it's solution is so weak that I had to take a star from the book's rating. Without giving anything away (I'll save that for the spoiler button in a minute), it's one of those very irritating mysteries where the culprit is only caught <i>because</i> they kept doing shit to scare someone off the case, like every villain in every episode of <i>Scooby-Do</i> ever. Stroud's villain gives those guys a run for their money in the scaring-people-off-the-case-and-therefore-helping-them-solve-it department. We eventually find out that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the guy hired Lockwood &amp; Co to investigate the house because he hoped that the ghosts would murder them. This is completely stupid, especially because he had no reason to be worried in the first place. The big important evidence he was trying to keep hidden? It's a coded inscription on the victim's locket, and once the kids figure it out they're like, aha, we've got you now! But all the inscription proves is that the guy was having an affair with the victim. We've still got a fifty-year-old cold case, no witnesses, and the body and the crime scene were destroyed in a fire. There's literally <i>zero proof</i> that the guy is a murderer, but he decides to be clever and kill the kids off, and that's how he gets caught, and it's so stupid and clumsy and it hurts my mystery-loving heart. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The book can almost function on its own as a story, although there's some setup for a sequel at the end, hinting that we're going to learn more about Lucy's abilities and the origins of the Problem. I'll have to track down Book 2 as soon as I can.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17093324436089068407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1986933569" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1986933569" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42163117-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508217767p2/42163117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1986933569?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/42163117-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1986933569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10097625568408235863">I was really excited to start this series, because <i>someone</i> <s>*cough* Sana</s> had hyped it up so much. Needless to say, it more than met those expectations. <br/><br/><i>The Screaming Staircase</i> follows the story of a team of teenage ghosthunters, set in an AU London plagued by dangerous paranormal apparitions. It was somehow fun and cute and creepy all at the same time. I don’t read very much middle grade, and I appreciated that while this was easy to read and its content is appropriate for a younger audience, Str</span>
  <span id="freeText10097625568408235863" style="display:none">I was really excited to start this series, because <i>someone</i> <s>*cough* Sana</s> had hyped it up so much. Needless to say, it more than met those expectations. <br /><br /><i>The Screaming Staircase</i> follows the story of a team of teenage ghosthunters, set in an AU London plagued by dangerous paranormal apparitions. It was somehow fun and cute and creepy all at the same time. I don’t read very much middle grade, and I appreciated that while this was easy to read and its content is appropriate for a younger audience, Stroud doesn’t write down to his readers. As C.S. Lewis said, “A children's story that can only be enjoyed by children is not a good children's story in the slightest,” and I couldn’t agree more.<br /><br />The characters were all so well-crafted and precious, and definitely the highlight of the book for me. I loved Lockwood, Lucy, and George all individually, but they also had fantastic group chemistry. They’re sweet and funny and brave, and I just want to hug them all <s>and also hire them the next time I’m home alone at night and start hearing strange noises.</s><br /><br />Additionally, the worldbuilding was fantastic—<i>Lockwood &amp; Co.</i>’s London is both similar and eerily different from our own. The level of detail provided about the history of the hauntings and the ways society has adapted to living among ghosts was fascinating. I also liked that there was actually a reason for such young protagonists to have so much responsibility in this system: as children and teens are far more sensitive to paranormal activity, it makes sense for them to be so capable and involved.<br /><br />Alright, confession time: this book was <i>slightly</i> terrifying because I am very easily scared by anything to do with ghost stories, and horror in general. I thought it would be okay because this is middle grade…..but it was still lowkey pretty scary <s> and I couldn't read it at night bc of my overactive and paranoid imagination</s>. (Disclaimer: I am <i>extremely</i> susceptible to anything scary, so anyone else who reads this will probably be fine.) Regardless of its scary-ness, I still loved this, and I can’t wait to get my hands on the next book in the series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10097625568408235863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2108099349" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15577038176768955669">London has been plagued by ghosts for more than half a century. Those with hauntings turn to psychic investigator agencies to help them. Several such agencies operate in London. Lucy Carlyle came to London in hopes of joining a prestigious agency to fight the spirits. But....she ended up at the low end of the industry. Lockwood & Company is the smallest and most beleaguered agency in the city. In fact, the company has one last chance to prove itself, or be defunct. Their last chance is a doozy -</span>
  <span id="freeText15577038176768955669" style="display:none">London has been plagued by ghosts for more than half a century. Those with hauntings turn to psychic investigator agencies to help them. Several such agencies operate in London. Lucy Carlyle came to London in hopes of joining a prestigious agency to fight the spirits. But....she ended up at the low end of the industry. Lockwood &amp; Company is the smallest and most beleaguered agency in the city. In fact, the company has one last chance to prove itself, or be defunct. Their last chance is a doozy -- spend the night in one of the most haunted residences in London and come out alive. <br /><br />Can they do it?<br /><br />I'm not going to give away much of the plot....no spoilers from me. But I will say the story moves at a steady pace. The action and scares are wonderfully fun. The humor is witty and the characters engaging. This book was just fun to read, especially now that the weather is cooling down and I'm starting to think Halloween-y thoughts. This was a nice book to kick off the fright season. :)<br /><br />The Screaming Staircase is a great start to the Lockwood &amp; Company series. Witty humor, scary ghosts, and mysteries to solve -- a great mix for a middle grade book series! There are currently four books in the series, with a fifth book, The Empty Grave, coming out soon. My 6th grader wanted to read something scary this Fall leading up to Halloween. I'm definitely steering him towards this series. I think he will love it! Nice mix of humor and scary. :) A fun read for any age....I'm definitely going to read the rest of the series. :)<br /><br />For more information on author Jonathan Stroud and his books, check out his website: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jonathanstroud.com/">http://www.jonathanstroud.com/</a></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_640115023" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/640115023" />
    <a title="Betsy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/221050-betsy"><img alt="Betsy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442631153p2/221050.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/640115023?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Betsy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Betsy" href="/user/show/221050-betsy">Betsy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/221050-betsy?shelf=mysteries">mysteries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/221050-betsy?shelf=creepy-books">creepy-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/221050-betsy?shelf=funny-fiction">funny-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/221050-betsy?shelf=ghost-stories">ghost-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/221050-betsy?shelf=british-imports">british-imports</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/221050-betsy?shelf=middle-grade-fantasy">middle-grade-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/221050-betsy?shelf=scary-books">scary-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/221050-betsy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/221050-betsy?shelf=alternate-worlds">alternate-worlds</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/221050-betsy?shelf=supernatural-mysteries">supernatural-mysteries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer640115023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2630436311401870468">I’m sick of historical fiction. I’m sick of contemporary fiction. I’m sick of realism and science fiction. Fantasy I watch with a wary eye. I don’t always feel this way but when I’ve read seven depressing meaningful middle grade books for kids in a row the old noggin screams for something enjoyable for once. And to place into this mental desert a book like <i>The Screaming Staircase</i> ... well, it’s the best possible cure for what ails ye. A pleasure from tip to tail, this is the book you hand the ad</span>
  <span id="freeText2630436311401870468" style="display:none">I’m sick of historical fiction. I’m sick of contemporary fiction. I’m sick of realism and science fiction. Fantasy I watch with a wary eye. I don’t always feel this way but when I’ve read seven depressing meaningful middle grade books for kids in a row the old noggin screams for something enjoyable for once. And to place into this mental desert a book like <i>The Screaming Staircase</i> ... well, it’s the best possible cure for what ails ye. A pleasure from tip to tail, this is the book you hand the advanced readers that claim they’d rather read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15997.Paradise_Lost" title="Paradise Lost by John Milton" rel="nofollow noopener">Paradise Lost</a> than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3.Harry_Potter_and_the_Sorcerer_s_Stone__Harry_Potter___1_" title="Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone (Harry Potter, #1) by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter</a>. Smart as a whip, funny, witty, and honestly frightening at times, Stroud lets loose and gives readers exactly what they want. Ghosts, kids on their own without adult supervision, and loads of delicious cookies.<br />	<br />It all began with The Problem. One day, for no apparent reason, the dead started to walk amongst the living. Not just walk, but really wreak some serious havoc. Here are the facts of the matter. 1. If you see a ghost, run. 2. Don’t let a ghost touch you, or you’re dead. 3. Only kids can see ghosts. What are we to make of these facts? Well, it’s no surprise when ghost-busting operations hiring children start cropping up. Enter Lockwood &amp; Company. Run by the charming Anthony Lockwood alongside his two compatriots Lucy and George the ramshackle operation is barely scraping by. Enter a job that goes particularly wrong when the kids accidentally burn down their employers’ home, and it would take a miracle to save the agency. Fortunately, a miracle shows up in the form of a very rich and powerful man. He’s hiring the three to take on the most haunted house in all of Britain. The catch? No one’s ever gotten out of it alive. Will our intrepid heroes take on the job, or is there more at work here than meets the eye?<br />	<br />There is no debate surrounding the joy one feels when reading this book. It is already beloved. Even without his popular Bartimaeus series, Stroud could have debuted with <i>The Screaming Staircase</i> and garnered legions of fans upon impact. That is not to say that it is without debate, however. Indeed, there is one point of contention that is raised when people learn of this book. In a word: audience. Can one honestly hand this book to a savvy 11-year-old reader without so much as a blink, or should you give it to a teen instead? In my experience I’ve noticed that before people have read the book they look at it and instantly assume it’s YA (young adult). Whether it’s the plot description or the cover or what have you it seems teen to them. However, once they’ve actually sat down and read the book cover to cover, most folks I’ve spoken to agree that it’s just fine for the juvenile crowd. Is there more blood than you can shake a stick at? Sure. But it’s ghost blood. Hardly the same thing. The closest thing I can compare it to is Joseph Delaney’s first book in The Last Apprentice series, <a href="http://fusenumber8.blogspot.com/2006/02/review-of-day-revenge-of-witch.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Revenge of the Witch</a>. Scary but not inappropriate, which is a delicate line to walk. It doesn’t hurt matters any that the kids in this book never give their ages. They’re on the cusp of adolescence, sure, but the fact that there are no allusions to crushes or palpitations of the heart is significant in its absence. It’s kind of the perfect thing to hand that kid who can’t stand even a whiff of romance in their fiction. <br />	<br />At its heart this is a great book to scare a kid with. Over the years I’ve noticed that love of horror begins at a very young age and never seems to go away. I used to have a four-year-old come to my reference desk in the library over and over asking for “scary” books. Pretty much as long as I could hand him something with a vampire or a monster on the cover, he was content. Once they start reading on their own, many kids gravitate to the Goosebumps section of their library. Low-key horror thrills, tailor made for the 7-10 year-old set. But as with all things, kids outgrow fads. They find Goosebumps babyish. They want something with a little more bite. So rather than hand them <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9460487.Miss_Peregrine_s_Home_for_Peculiar_Children__Miss_Peregrine___1_" title="Miss Peregrine's Home for Peculiar Children (Miss Peregrine, #1) by Ransom Riggs" rel="nofollow noopener">Miss Peregrine's Home for Peculiar Children</a> quite yet, I need something that will run a finger down their spines without tripping wholly into teen territory. In the past the aforementioned <i>Revenge of the Witch</i> was my go to book. Now <i>The Screaming Staircase</i> will serve just as nicely.<br />	<br />One point that I’m in danger of not mentioning is the fact that the book is bloody funny. Who else could get away with a sentence like, "..George Cubbins, handsome as a freshly opened tub of margarine, as charismatic as a wet tea towel lying scrumpled on the floor”? Scrumpled. Delicious. Actually, Stroud is at his best when Lucy is describing George. “With his glasses off, his eyes looked small and weak – blinky and a bit baffled, like an unintelligent sheep that’s taken a wrong turn. But when he put them on again, they went all sharp and steely, more like the eyes of an eagle that eats dumb sheep for breakfast.” All throughout the story you are in Lucy’s head and though she is allowed to make her own fair share of stupid mistakes (no Hermione Granger she, thank heavens), you like her snarky sense of the absurd. Lucy actually acts as a kind of Watson to Lockwood’s Holmes, but not the bumbling Watson we’re so familiar with these days. She’s got a good head on her shoulders. You come to like her compatriots too, for that matter. A wittier crew you won’t find this year.<br />	<br />Above and beyond the humor, however, there’s much to be said for Stroud’s actual writing. As I mentioned before, you love the characters. The plot and mystery components play fair (and I admit that I didn’t suspect the true villain of the piece when I probably should have). But it’s the wordplay that gets me. Consider a sentence like this: “In fact, it wasn’t at all an ugly hallway; in bright sunlight it might have looked quite pleasant. But not so much now, with the last light from the door panes stretching out like skewed coffins on the floor in front of us; and with our shadows neatly framed inside them..” Or, later, my favorite part is when Lucy is naming her old partners in the ghost busting business. “We worked together. We had fun. We saved each other’s lives a bit. Their names, if you’re interested, were Paul, Norrie, Julie, Steph, and Alfie-Joe. They’re all dead now.” It’s just a little twist of the knife, but it gets the job done.<br />	<br />There are some moments of British-to-American translation that rankled me but will pass unnoticed by the general child population. Lucy is continually talking about “tea and cookies”, a phrase guaranteed to jar in the head of this particular Anglophile. My suspicion is that this was a true “tea and biscuit” book from start to finish, but that biscuits have an entirely different connotation in the States and as a result the word was switched. Other switches passed me by unnoticed, which is to their credit. Pity about the cookies. Still, it’s a remarkably mild complaint to make. Cookies schmookies. The book’s a pip.<br />	<br />You would be forgiven for thinking this book a work of historical fantasy fiction, were it not informing you left and right of its contemporary nature. Velcro holds the rapiers in place, for example. In another moment a television is mentioned. Yet there’s something classic in its form. I suppose you could technically call the story post-apocalyptic, if you consider the apocalypse in question The Problem. You could call it a straight up horror story. Or you could turn around and label it a mystery. And what about fantasy? It’s definitely in that genre as well. Howsoever you feel like labeling it, there’s one thing you can certainly label the book: good. It’s a delight from start to finish and after you’ve devoured it you find yourself craving more more more. For everyone then. Child, teen, adult, or slow shuffling specter, this is a book for you. Try it on for size.<br /><br />For ages 10 and up.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2630436311401870468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2143686403" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2143686403" />
    <a title="Jody " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41767362-jody"><img alt="Jody " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558120407p2/41767362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2143686403?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jody " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jody " href="/user/show/41767362-jody">Jody </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23923511-the-screaming-staircase">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41767362-jody?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41767362-jody?shelf=spooktacular">spooktacular</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2143686403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9256037453107148527">What a fun and hauntingly great time this was. I decided to try Jonathan Stroud's <i>The Screaming Staircase</i> for one of my Spooktacular Halloween reads. After finishing this first book, I may just have to read the entire series right away. <br/><br/>The setting is London, England and this is not the London we know today. For the last 50 years there has been a problem with ghosts and hauntings. This has been named easily enough <i>The Problem</i>. See the thing about ghosts in this world is they can only be seen by </span>
  <span id="freeText9256037453107148527" style="display:none">What a fun and hauntingly great time this was. I decided to try Jonathan Stroud's <i>The Screaming Staircase</i> for one of my Spooktacular Halloween reads. After finishing this first book, I may just have to read the entire series right away. <br /><br />The setting is London, England and this is not the London we know today. For the last 50 years there has been a problem with ghosts and hauntings. This has been named easily enough <i>The Problem</i>. See the thing about ghosts in this world is they can only be seen by kids or young adults. Once a person reaches adulthood they can no longer see or sense ghosts. So, the only people left to tackle the ghost problem are the younger generation. <br /><br />In steps our main character and ghost psychic Lucy Carlyle. Lucy has the ability to hear ghosts and she also can sense their emotions at times. This is knows as <i>Talent</i>. Most children are born with a <i>Talent</i>, but they may be sensitive to sight or touch. There are many agencies set up throughout London that employ children and adult supervisors that specialize in fighting <i>The Problem</i> with the ghosts. Lucy is the newest member of the smallest agency known as Lockwood &amp; Co. The agency is made up of 3 employees: Anthony Lockwood, George Cubbins, and Lucy Carlyle. <br /><br />The story follows Lucy, Lockwood, and George on their ghost fighting adventures. There are plenty of creepy moments, close calls, and intense scenes. Also, a surprising twist I didn't catch until the last minute. The story was a mixture of ghost hunting and murder mystery, and the two were intertwined very well. <br /><br />Mr. Stroud did a great job with the terminology and atmosphere of the book. The terms like creeping fear, dark specter, and raw-bones help give the story an ominous feel. The book is geared more toward middle grade readers, but it was really good for some creepy moments while reading at night. <br /><br /><i>The Screaming Staircase</i> was exactly what I was looking for in a October/Halloween read. Great story, great characters, and most of all spook factor. I highly recommend this book to readers of all ages. <br /><br />4 stars **** </span>
  <a data-text-id="9256037453107148527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1069277871?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darth J " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darth J " href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j">Darth J </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Darth J  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/7897213-andrea-ninja-bunneh">Andrea ❤Ninja Bunneh❤</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1069277871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13318846465109341405">3.75 stars<br/><br/>*Please note that an Amazon seller sent me an uncorrected ARC of this instead of the hardcover I actually ordered so the book I read may be different than the final product.*<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413301293i/11492530._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Initially I liked the concept of this book: young, psychic ghost-hunting sleuths who use an array of gadgets to solve mysteries in haunted houses. The problem is that the writing is sometimes too dry to keep your attention. Though the dialogue is realistic for the characters, not the overly snarky way adults writer</span>
  <span id="freeText13318846465109341405" style="display:none">3.75 stars<br><br>*Please note that an Amazon seller sent me an uncorrected ARC of this instead of the hardcover I actually ordered so the book I read may be different than the final product.*<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413301293i/11492530._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Initially I liked the concept of this book: young, psychic ghost-hunting sleuths who use an array of gadgets to solve mysteries in haunted houses. The problem is that the writing is sometimes too dry to keep your attention. Though the dialogue is realistic for the characters, not the overly snarky way adults writers think teens speak but intelligent yet somewhat flawed in their rationalizations.<br><br>The world building is roughly half telling and half showing, but there is plenty of background to slog through until you get to the meat of the story. The first mention of the Screaming Staircase (you know, the subject of the title?) happens when the novel is approximately 2/3 over. Until then, there is plenty to learn about the ghosts in this world like how they are categorized (which is somewhat vague) and what materials are used to contain them/keep them at bay.<br><br>Probably the scariest moment in this novel is when the trio find their house has been broken into and are faced by an assailant wielding a rapier and wearing a “white cloth mask [with] eye sockets [of] black slashed holes [and] another slash, jagged and off-center, formed the mouth.” (p. 205)<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413301293i/11492532._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There were times I’ve wanted to give up on this book, but the thing that really kept me going was seeing the intriguing cover of the sequel. This novel could have been campy and gone in a very Scooby Doo direction, but I’m glad it didn’t. I don’t like the horror-comedy hybrid genre as a rule and that would have turned me off completely. What you have here is a dark MG novel that takes itself with the appropriate amount of seriousness.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13318846465109341405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1919576031" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1919576031" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56485897-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532735871p2/56485897.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1919576031?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/56485897-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781423164913" href="/book/show/17428653-the-screaming-staircase">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">EVERYONE</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Alyssa by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/26402455-sana">Sana</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56485897-alyssa?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56485897-alyssa?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1919576031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4482155936762390219"><b>4.5 Lockwood Stars!</b><br/><br/><b>Rating:</b> ★ ★ ★ ★ and a half / 5 stars<br/><b>Lead Male Character:</b> ★ ★ ★ ★ and a half / 5 stars (Lockwood and George)<br/><b>Lead Female Character:</b> ★ ★ ★ ★ / 5 stars<br/><b>Plotline:</b> ★ ★ ★ ★ and a half / 5 stars <br/><b>Genre:</b> Thriller, mystery, adventure, action, middle-grade<br/><b>Will I recommend this book to others?:</b> YES<br/><b>Will I reread this book?:</b> YES <br/><b>Overall story summed up in one word:</b> Brilliant! <br/><br/><b>Minor Spoilers Ahead!</b><br/><br/>Sauna, I thank you for recommending me this book because it was beyond brilliant! I haven't read </span>
  <span id="freeText4482155936762390219" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Lockwood Stars!</b><br /><br /><b>Rating:</b> ★ ★ ★ ★ and a half / 5 stars<br /><b>Lead Male Character:</b> ★ ★ ★ ★ and a half / 5 stars (Lockwood and George)<br /><b>Lead Female Character:</b> ★ ★ ★ ★ / 5 stars<br /><b>Plotline:</b> ★ ★ ★ ★ and a half / 5 stars <br /><b>Genre:</b> Thriller, mystery, adventure, action, middle-grade<br /><b>Will I recommend this book to others?:</b> YES<br /><b>Will I reread this book?:</b> YES <br /><b>Overall story summed up in one word:</b> Brilliant! <br /><br /><b>Minor Spoilers Ahead!</b><br /><br />Sauna, I thank you for recommending me this book because it was beyond brilliant! I haven't read a book like this in a while that I just couldn't put down and had to keep reading! I love you so much! &lt;3<br /><br /> <b>Likes</b><br /><br />I actually loved a lot about this book and I'm surprised because this book is considered "middle-grade" and I'm past that age level. I went into this book thinking that it was going to be OK and another one of those slow stories, but boy was I wrong! From a little bit after the beginning until the end, it was filled with action-packed scenes and lots of wonderful surprises. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13555073.The_Screaming_Staircase__Lockwood___Co____1_" title="The Screaming Staircase (Lockwood &amp; Co., #1) by Jonathan Stroud" rel="nofollow noopener">The Screaming Staircase</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/33467.Jonathan_Stroud" title="Jonathan Stroud" rel="nofollow noopener">Jonathan Stroud</a> is definitely something I'd recommend to those looking for a good middle-grade thriller novel. <br /><br /><b>Anthony Lockwood</b> is my <b>husband</b>. Sauna, you have to share because I want him too! Called "Lockwood" by all his peers, he is someone <b>super fascinating</b>. He's smart, unique, and has a passion for what he does and I admire that about him. Lockwood takes his job really seriously and does it with his absolute best and I have to say it again, I love that about him. Though his past remains unknown to us as well as a lot of his motives, it doesn't matter because his banter and love for Lucy and George rises above that. He doesn't say it outright, but you can tell he cares deeply for them two. Lockwood is also really brave and can take the lead in the dark and I think that's really <b>hot</b>, LOL. I know for a fact that I cannot have this job, because 1) I am <s>afraid</s> of the dark and 2) Hell, I'm a scaredy pants. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>...Ah, here's your weak-bladdered friend back. About time too. <br /><br />Lockwood was pattering toward us, a spring in his step. Sorry about that, he said. Have I missed anything?</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Lucy Carlyle</b> is a somewhat <b>boring</b> character. I'm going to talk more about this in the "Dislikes" section of this review so I'm just going to be brief here: Lucy shouldn't have narrated this story. I would have prefer Lockwood, even George! Her backstory isn't interesting at all. Now, even though we also know nothing of Lockwood's history, there's just this <i>mysteriousness</i> to him that Lucy doesn't have. Maybe one main reason for that is because Lucy narrates versus Lockwood so we don't get to hear his thoughts as we do for Lucy. And she is pretty badass too, I have to admit. She is smart and knows what to do and what not to do in times of distress. <br /><br /> <b>
  <i>...BFF! That's Big Fat Foot, by the way.</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>George</b>, does he have a last name? I <b>love</b> this guy. He's snarky, sarcastic, and like Lockwood, equally mysterious. <i>How did he and Lockwood meet?</i> <i>Has he got any family?</i> You know, things like that. I do feel, however, that George is even more unknown than Lockwood. We don't know a lot about him and I really hope his backstory is explained into further detail in the coming books. George is my <b>second favorite character</b> in this book after Lockwood and before Lucy. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Take his appearance. There was something about it that acted as a trigger to one's worst instincts. His was was uniquely slappable while his backside cried out to heaven for a well-placed kick. He slouched, he slumped, he scuffed his way about the house... And that flop of hair! And those silly glasses! Everything about him irritated me.</i>
</b><br />George is just so cute! &lt;3<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Then he took hold of the handle and pushed, and the horror of the night began.</i>
</b> <br /><br /> <b>Dislikes</b><br /><br />Though this story has many good aspects to it, they were, in fact, some things that threw me off and annoyed me. Starting off, the POV (point of view). The Screaming Staircase is told in Lucy's POV, first person. And I hated it because we don't get to hear Lockwood and George's thoughts. I would have much preferred the book be in <b>third person</b> and switched between the characters. That way, I would have been able to get a feel of all the characters and their reactions and feelings throughout, not just Lucy. <br /><br />Something else that bothered me deeply was the fact that <i>The Screaming Staircase</i> only consisted of the last 75 or so pages. The book is called <i>The Screaming Staircase</i>, though we read more about it at the very end. Personally, I don't feel that that is an appropriate title for the book. Maybe something that mentions the overall house (where the staircase is located in) or something about the Red Room. <br /><br />Also, I feel that the first 50 or so pages of the book could've been cut off. I didn't really care for the very beginning since very little happens then. All the action starts around the middle and the author could've jumped straight into that, rather than drag on the story. <br /><br /> <b>Overall</b><br /><br />A great thriller and something I'd recommend and reread in the future! <br /><br />~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ <br /><br />Recommended to me by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/26402455-sana-khalid" rel="nofollow noopener">Sauna</a>! I really hope I <s>don't</s> like it <s>because Sauna always trashes on everyone's favorite books and I really want to do it back to her on her favorite series</s> because then I can finally fangirl with Sauna *waggles eyebrows* :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="4482155936762390219" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/705918579" />
    <a title="Tiff" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3158351-tiff"><img alt="Tiff" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372086741p2/3158351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/705918579?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiff" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiff" href="/user/show/3158351-tiff">Tiff</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780857532022" href="/book/show/17612879-the-screaming-staircase">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3158351-tiff?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3158351-tiff?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer705918579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18287552716746202808">I have two confessions...<br/><br/>1) I have NEVER read a Jonathan Stroud book before. I am aware this is a shocking error and shall have to be rectified before I end up in library purgatory.<br/><br/>2) I am a complete scaredy cat and do not read ghost stories.<br/><br/>So, when I received a review copy of Lockwood I was...unsure to say the least, but I thought give it a go - expand your reading horizons, and I am SO glad I did.<br/><br/>Ghosts are real. The Problem is widespread with many reports of Visitors and fatal cases of ghost</span>
  <span id="freeText18287552716746202808" style="display:none">I have two confessions...<br /><br />1) I have NEVER read a Jonathan Stroud book before. I am aware this is a shocking error and shall have to be rectified before I end up in library purgatory.<br /><br />2) I am a complete scaredy cat and do not read ghost stories.<br /><br />So, when I received a review copy of Lockwood I was...unsure to say the least, but I thought give it a go - expand your reading horizons, and I am SO glad I did.<br /><br />Ghosts are real. The Problem is widespread with many reports of Visitors and fatal cases of ghost-touch. In order to deal with The Problem, agencies started springing up, staffed by...well...children to assist the haunted. One such agency is Lockwood &amp; Co. The book follows the Lockwood team on several of their cases.<br /><br />I loved loved loved this book! It is exciting and unputdownable. The writing is utterly brilliant and so engaging I was drawn into the story from the start. The characters are fab, each with their own talents and strengths and equally needed to succeed as a team. I particularly like the charismatic Lockwood who I see as a young Cumberbatch!<br /><br />The book was scary, with several scenes that left me wincing with quite vivid mental pictures - but as I said, I'm a big softy. I cannot wait to read more in this series, Lockwood is one of my best books of the year. <br /><br />Thank you for the review copy, I'm off now to seek out Bartimaeus!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18287552716746202808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BtHfbkPSbUUsDyMOJK/BWqR73vysGDHFi/uB4DGdo48897a8+IykLYskl2/TWsuFciQ5NGKVv6LQhcdR/N5RFQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EHW+yodOZplWxzs7BDokW/SijqxxPh1nVVzYEz8wbEwqU9cYPBCv8fHsj1rzzy6EIv1pZL+zkwAOIp6i8nOe1g==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10746031595407951543">Jonathan Anthony Stroud is an author of fantasy books, mainly for children and youths.<br/><br/>Stroud grew up in St Albans where he enjoyed reading books, drawing pictures, and writing stories. Between the ages seven and nine he was often ill, so he spent most of his days in the hospital or in his bed at home. To escape boredom he would occupy himself with books and stories. After he completed his studies </span>
  <span id="freeText10746031595407951543" style="display:none">Jonathan Anthony Stroud is an author of fantasy books, mainly for children and youths.<br /><br />Stroud grew up in St Albans where he enjoyed reading books, drawing pictures, and writing stories. Between the ages seven and nine he was often ill, so he spent most of his days in the hospital or in his bed at home. To escape boredom he would occupy himself with books and stories. After he completed his studies of English literature at the University of York, he worked in London as an editor for the Walker Books store. He worked with different types of books there and this soon led to the writing of his own books. During the 1990s, he started publishing his own works and quickly gained success.<br /><br />In May 1999, Stroud published his first children's novel, Buried Fire, which was the first of a line of fantasy/mythology children's books.<br /><br />Among his most prominent works are the bestselling Bartimaeus Trilogy. A special feature of these novels compared to others of their genre is that Stroud examines the stereotypes and ethics of the magician class and the enslaved demons. This is done by examining the perspective of the sarcastic and slightly egomaniacal djinni Bartimaeus. The books in this series are The Amulet of Samarkand, The Golem's Eye, and Ptolemy's Gate, his first books to be published in the United States. <br /><br />Stroud lives in St Albans, Hertfordshire, with his two children, Isabelle and Arthur, and his wife Gina, an illustrator of children's books.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10746031595407951543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
